(2) Next Monday's Central Commemoration Week will be reported on by Committee Member Ye Chucang. (3) The National Revolutionary Army Oath-Taking Commemoration on July 9 will be reported on by Committee Member Zhu Peide. Other routine cases. (4th Central News Agency dispatch)

Legislative Yuan Reviews Penalties for Undermining National Currency 48

(Nanjing) The Legislative Yuan reviewed the draft regulations on penalties for undermining national currency on the 4th. Chen Changheng, Wei Tingsheng, Zheng Hongnian, Liu Yaojun, Luo Ding, and others attended. Dai Mingli, section chief of the Currency Department of the Ministry of Finance, was present to explain. As a result of the review, amendments were passed and submitted to the general assembly. The content deals with the destruction of national currency or the use of opportunities for speculation and manipulation to depreciate the price of national currency, and imposes sentences of imprisonment of up to five years, depending on the severity of the case. (4th special dispatch)

(Nanjing) Regarding the case of strict punishment for undermining the national currency, the principles were repeatedly resolved by the Central Political Council and sent by the National Government to the Legislative Yuan for compliance. Subsequently, the Legislative Yuan and Kong Xiangxi submitted opinions to the Central Government on the case one after another, which were again discussed by the Central Political Council. All the members believed that the government's policy of abolishing taels and adopting yuan was not implemented for long. However, some unscrupulous merchants tried to profit and destroyed national currency in batches to privately mint silver ingots and precious silver. Moreover, they took advantage of the rising world silver prices to smuggle them abroad for sale. Currently, many such cases have been cracked, and the impact is that the losses suffered by the national treasury are not small, and the currency will never be stable. During this transition period, a separate set of regulations should be formulated to strictly ban and remedy this situation. At the same time, Kong Xiangxi submitted a draft of the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Acts Undermining National Currency, which was resolved and passed by the Central Political Council and submitted to the Legislative Yuan for review. Sun Ke instructed the Finance and Criminal Law Committees of the Yuan to expedite the review and report. The two committees held a joint meeting for review on the afternoon of the 4th. More than ten committee members, including Liu Kejun, attended. Chen Changheng was the acting chairman. The Ministry of Finance also sent personnel to attend and explain. As a result, the seven articles of the Provisional Regulations for Punishing Acts Undermining National Currency were amended and passed and submitted for deliberation at the Yuan meeting on the morning of the 5th. In addition, the Accounting Law and the Fujian-Guangdong Construction Public Price Case have also been included in the agenda for the meeting on the 5th. (4th Central News Agency dispatch)

Ministry of Finance Formulates Measures to Organize Cash Revenue and Expenditure 49

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance stipulates that the cash revenue and expenditure of various financial institutions that belong to the institutions themselves are based on the date when the revenue and expenditure accounts are realized and included in the report for that period, while the revenue and expenditure of subordinate institutions are based on the date of reporting and included in the report for the reporting period. As a result, at the end of each year, a portion of the revenue and expenditure of subordinate institutions is included in the accounts and reports of the next year as revenue and expenditure for the next year, and the content of the annual report is not sufficient to reflect the actual revenue and expenditure of the institution and its subordinate institutions for the entire year. Therefore, ten measures for organizing cash revenue and expenditure have been formulated and issued to subordinate units for compliance. (4th Central News Agency dispatch)

Directorate General of Posts Establishes Design Committee 50

(Nanjing) The Directorate General of Posts has submitted a request to the Ministry of Communications to establish a design committee to plan postal improvement and development. It is scheduled to be established within the month. The ten articles of the regulations were announced on the 4th. (4th special dispatch)

(Nanjing) Last year, the Directorate General of Posts borrowed 1 million yuan from the Reserve Exchange Bureau to build post offices in various places. The Jiaotong Building was first built in Nanchang. After the project was completed, the Wuchang and Shanghai Central Exchange Bureaus will be completed in two months. Drawings have been made, bids have been invited, and construction has begun. The Changsha Administration Bureau can be completed this year. The Sanya Administration Bureau of Hainan Province will be built in advance, and the Savings and Exchange Bureau will continue to provide funds to handle the matter. (4th special dispatch)

Central Propaganda Committee Plans to Reorganize; Shanghai Book Review Committee; Director and Reviewers of Publications Dismissed for Negligence 51

(Nanjing) Regarding the publication of the article "Idle Talk About the Emperor" in the 15th issue of the second volume of Shanghai New Life Weekly, after the Japanese side filed a protest, the Shanghai Municipal Government immediately suspended the publication of New Life Weekly and handed it over to the court for legal processing, and prohibited newspapers and magazines from reprinting the text. At the same time, the mayor expressed his apology. The Central Propaganda Committee noted that Shanghai had a book and magazine review committee responsible for reviewing the original manuscripts. It also paid special attention to this case. In addition to informing the party headquarters of all provinces and cities by telegram to work with the government to strictly investigate, ban, and detain the publication, and notifying the party headquarters of all provinces and cities separately to strictly crack down on similar incidents in the future, the committee believed that the book and magazine review committee failed to report the incident, which was a serious negligence, and decided to dismiss the director and reviewers of the review group and plan to reorganize. (4th Central News Agency dispatch)

Communist Party; Yuan Shu's Investigation Completed; Original Text of the Indictment by the Hubei High Prosecutor 52

(Hankou) Yuan Shu, who was arrested in connection with the case of the strange Westerner and the Communist Party, has been escorted from Shanghai to Hubei for interrogation. It has now been learned that Yuan Shu confessed that he was absorbed by the Communist Party organization due to his leftist ideology and was responsible for promoting communism. He also submitted a declaration of self-confession, describing in detail his leftist ideology and his experience of joining the Communist Party. The court has now concluded its investigation and believes that there is indeed evidence of promoting doctrines incompatible with the Three Principles of the People. He is being prosecuted in accordance with Article 6 of the Emergency Law for Punishing Acts Endangering the Republic of China. The original text of the indictment has been obtained and is recorded below. Indictment by the Prosecutor of the Hubei High Court. Defendant: Yuan Shu, male, 25 years old, editor of the Foreign Commentary Translation Agency, residing in Shanghai. The defendant listed on the right is being prosecuted for endangering the Republic of China. The facts of the crime, evidence, and applicable legal articles are listed below. (1) Facts of the Crime: Defendant Yuan Shu is also known as Yuan Xueyi and Yuan Xiaoyi. He received a considerable education. Due to his poor family background and heavy burden, he contributed to newspapers to make a living. He initially approached anarchists and participated in the "Black Youth" movement. He already harbored a sense of hatred towards society. Later, reading social science books aroused his leftist ideology. Because he had a considerable knowledge of journalism, he gathered young leftist elements and founded the Literary and News Weekly. His work was entirely centered on the leftist cultural movement. In the winter of 1931, the date is unknown, when foreign aggression and internal troubles occurred, the defendant was motivated by fanaticism and excitement, believing that only the Communist Party could save China from danger. He often made radical remarks. At that time, the leftist cultural movement developed more and more, and the defendant's appeal to the strength of the young masses became greater and greater, so he was absorbed by the Communist Party organization and served as the editor-in-chief of the Chinese edition of the China Forum Weekly, engaging in communist propaganda work. He also received special training. In May of this year, Joseph Gredon, the head of the Communist Party's Third International Shanghai office, was arrested in Shanghai. The defendant's name and address were found. After receiving the news, the defendant went to the Shanghai Garrison Headquarters on the 23rd of the same month to surrender himself. After being interrogated and suspected of being a Communist Party member, he was escorted here. During the investigation, the defendant submitted a declaration of self-confession. The investigation by this court is as described above. (2) Evidence of the Crime and Applicable Legal Articles: The above facts are described in detail in the defendant's declaration of self-confession and repeatedly confessed during the investigation, which can be taken as evidence. The materials collected by the China Forum Weekly are entirely propaganda for communism, which has been clarified by the defendant. Therefore, his promotion of communism, which is incompatible with the Three Principles of the People, for the purpose of endangering the Republic of China, is very obvious. In light of his actions, he is a joint offender of Article 6 of the Emergency Law for Punishing Acts Endangering the Republic of China in accordance with Articles 11 and 28 of the Criminal Law. He is prosecuted in accordance with Article 1 of the Implementing Regulations of the same law, Article 230, Paragraph 1, and Article 243 of the Criminal Procedure Law. (4th Central News Agency dispatch)

Interpretation of Whether Crimes and Punishments under the Old Criminal Law Should Be Executed 67

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Justice previously received a request from the Shandong High Court for an interpretation of whether crimes and punishments imposed under the old Criminal Law's Article 288 and Article 289, etc., on conspiracy crimes, and the Regulations on Punishing Evil Gentry, etc., before the implementation of the new Criminal Law should be exempted from execution. The ministry explained that although the new Criminal Law does not have special articles on conspiracy offenders, their actions should still be punished as instigation or assistance, depending on the circumstances, and should not be exempted from execution in accordance with the provisions of Article 2, Paragraph 3 of the Criminal Law. As for those who have been sentenced to crimes under the Regulations on Punishing Evil Gentry, the Regulations on Punishing Kidnappers, and the Special Criminal False Accusation Punishment Law, the nature of the crimes committed under each article should be examined first. If the criminal behavior does not constitute a crime that is punishable under the criminal laws and regulations in effect at the time of the implementation of the new Criminal Law, it should be exempted from execution. The ministry has submitted this interpretation to the Judicial Yuan for approval and has issued a notice to all courts to comply with it. (4th Central News Agency dispatch)

A Record of Qu Qiubai's Execution: He Dreamed of Walking on a Mountain Path the Night Before His Execution; a Last Poem and Preface 87

A dispatch from Changting reports that after being captured by the 36th Division, Qu Qiubai, the former member of the Central Committee and Minister of Education of the Red Bandits, was imprisoned at the division headquarters in Changting for over a month. He received preferential treatment and was given a special cell. Qu was addicted to tobacco and alcohol, consuming a bottle of liquor daily and constantly smoking cigarettes. I visited him twice and saw him writing articles or carving seals at his desk. He wrote a booklet titled "Superfluous Words," filled with melancholy. He was fond of writing poetry, including poems like "Remembering Home," "Puzzled Feelings," and "Self-Deprecation," often quoting lines from Tang Dynasty poets. He carved no fewer than sixty seals, with elegant calligraphy. Qu's face was thin and pale, his body frail, and his head had well-developed nerves. In prison, he wore a blue cotton shirt and pants, resembling a merchant. He spoke with refinement, like a scholar. I had the following conversation with him: (Question) Mr. Qu, what are your thoughts on being captured this time? (Answer) I have been busy with the revolution all my life and longed for a short rest. Being imprisoned is what I expected. (Question) In your opinion, what led to the failure of the Red Bandits this time? (Answer) This failure is purely due to the success of the National Army's policy of "three parts military, seven parts political." The construction of blockhouses, roads, and material blockade also caused difficulties for the Red areas. (Question) Where is your wife, Yang Zhihua, and do you have any communication with her? (Answer) When I left Shanghai for Fujian last February, Yang originally intended to accompany me, but she couldn't due to illness. The situation in Shanghai has deteriorated this year, and the secret organizations have been completely destroyed. I fear she is also a prisoner. (Question) Will you change in any way in the future? (Answer) I am ultimately a scholar and love literature. I hope to translate more literary works in the future. (Question) What are your thoughts on pseudo-communism? Qu smiled without answering and took a drink. Knowing he didn't want to express anything, I excused myself.

On June 15th, Qu went to the New Life Club to read the newspaper. The guards closely attended him. He saw me again, nodded in greeting, and smiled amiably before busily reading the newspaper. I did not speak with him. On the 17th, he received a telegram from the central government ordering him to be executed on the spot. The next morning (the 18th) at 8 AM, Liao Xiangguang, the company commander of the special service company, went to the prison to take Qu to Zhongshan Park for a photograph. Qu gladly accompanied him. After the photo was taken, Commander Liao showed him the order. Qu nodded and said heroically, "Death is the greatest rest in life." Commander Liao asked if he had any last words. Qu replied, "I have a poem that I haven't written down yet." He returned to his cell, took up his brush, and wrote the following poem and preface: "Evening of June 17, 1935, I dreamed of walking on a mountain path. The setting sun flickered, and the cold stream gurgled, as if I were in a fairyland. The next day, reading a Tang Dynasty poem, I suddenly saw the line 'The setting sun flickers amid the chaotic mountains.' I then composed a poem with collected lines: 'The setting sun flickers amid the chaotic mountains; the falling leaves and cold spring sound different; I have endured ten years of loneliness; my heart holds half a verse of emptiness.' I was about to write it out

Page 10

when the order for my execution arrived. It is lamentable." Qiubai once wrote, "When the clouds and mist pass from my eyes, it will be my time of leisure." "These are not lyrics but words expressing my feelings in prison." Not signed, Qiubai's last writing completed. He then walked to Zhongshan Park, drank a catty of baijiu in a pavilion, talked and laughed freely, and sang the Russian Internationale and the Red Army Song, his voice trembling and barely audible. After singing, he slowly walked to the execution ground, holding a cigarette and remaining calm. Upon reaching the execution ground, he sat cross-legged on the grass, nodding and smiling. A moment later, a shot rang out, and he fell dead. The onlookers thronged the streets, expressing their satisfaction. The charges against him are listed below: "Regarding the announcement of the charges, the bandit leader Qu Qiubai joined the Communist Party in Moscow, Russia, in 1921 and has been working for the party ever since. In 1923, he was sent back to China to join our party, harboring sinister schemes to turn the whole country into a bandit state, and willingly becoming a dog for the Third International. After our National Revolutionary Army reached Wuhan in 1927, the bandit's schemes became increasingly exposed. The leaders of our party began to declare their opposition to communism with decisive measures. At that time, the bandit was in charge of the pseudo-Central Political Bureau, the highest leading organ of the bandit party. Seeing that his schemes were not succeeding, he advocated for adventurism, advocating for the seizure of power through bandit-style actions. As a result, countless innocent civilians in the provinces of Henan, Hubei, Hunan, Guangdong, Jiangxi, and Anhui were unjustly killed under his oppression and threats, numbering in the hundreds of thousands. The provinces suffered horrific destruction of burning and killing, which has its origins here. In 1928, the bandit returned to Russia, serving as a representative of the Chinese Communist Party. In 1930, he returned to China, still serving as a member of the pseudo-Central Committee, hiding in Shanghai and handling supplies to bandits in Jiangxi. Last February, he sneaked into Ruijin, serving as a pseudo-Education People's Commissioner of the bandit party, attempting to turn the children of Jiangxi and Fujian into bandits to serve as a bandit base. Last August, the main force of the bandit army fled westward, and the bandit stayed in the countryside of Ruijin, organizing a pseudo-Central Office to command the remnants of bandits in Fujian and Jiangxi to continue their harassment. This February, due to our army's suppression, he realized that his efforts would fail and attempted to move to Shanghai. On March 20th, he attempted to deceive us in the hope of being released, and only confessed after strict interrogation. In short, all the actions of the Communist bandits in various regions since 1927 are due to this bandit's instigation. The lives and property of the provinces of Jiangxi, Anhui, Fujian, Guangdong, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, and Sichuan have been directly or indirectly subjected to this bandit's killing and destruction, and the numbers cannot be counted. His crimes are heinous and unforgivable, especially since the bandit's conspiracies and disruptions have led to this □□□□, □□□□, even more so he is a thousand-year criminal against the country and the nation. It is not enough to eat his flesh and sleep on his skin to atone for his crimes. Fortunately, the bandit's brutal tricks have been witnessed by the people of the country and are intolerable to the world. That is why, over the years, through the efforts of our army and people in encirclement and suppression, most of them have been wiped out. Especially since the bandit was captured, the Communist bandits have lost their leadership, and the remaining bandits will easily be eliminated. The ministry reported to the chairman of the military committee, Chiang, for instructions, and received the winter telegram, 'Qu Qiubai to be executed by firing squad in Fujian and photographed for verification,' etc. In addition to verifying the bandit's identity and tying him to the execution ground for execution by firing squad, this proclamation is hereby issued so that the public knows. Bandit leader Qu Qiubai, 38 years old, from Changzhou, Jiangsu."

Photograph after Qu Qiubai's execution

Anhui Floods: River Tides and Mountain Torrents Surge; Xuanjing Suffers Flood Dragon, Inundating Tens of Thousands of Acres; Railway and Highway Damage Obstructs Traffic 88

A dispatch from Wuhu reports that in recent days, the counties of southern Anhui have experienced violent winds and heavy rains. The river tides have risen sharply, causing reverse flow, and mountain torrents have rushed down, causing the water level to increase by several feet. Although the weather has fortunately been clear and calm recently, the temperature has dropped, and the water volume continues to rise unabated. In the hinterland, Xuanzhou, Jingxian, and other places have experienced flood dragon disasters, with water flowing downstream and rising by more than three feet in a single day. As of last night, the water volume at the junction of the Wuhu inland river and the Yangtze River has reached 26 feet 5 inches on the customs water gauge, only four feet away from the great flood of 1931. Therefore, low-lying areas along the riverbanks of Nanmen and Jinmamen in Wuhu have been completely submerged. As for the embankments, the Wuzhang Lake in the fourth district, the Gaoyan, Zhangqiu, and Duxing dams in the sixth district, the Donghu beach in the seventh district, and the Zhucun embankment in the entrance district were breached last night due to the impact of mountain torrents, inundating more than 20,000 acres of farmland. Furthermore, Wan Chun and Xing Chun, each in the enclosure, have also experienced major dangers. The embankments encompass 80,000 to 90,000 acres of farmland, and thousands of people are working day and night to rescue them, with the situation extremely tense. Gao Wenbo, the commissioner of the Second District Administrative Inspectorate and concurrently the magistrate of Wuhu County, has led Construction Commissioner Hou Hongkai and hydraulic engineering personnel to inspect and assist in rescue efforts in various districts. He has also dispatched a large security team to garrison along the Yangtze River embankments, assisting the civilians in defense. Furthermore, the embankments along the west bank of Datong and Yuezizhou are of great importance to the water conservancy of Tongling, Shidai, and Qingyang. However, a portion of them suddenly collapsed the night before due to strong winds and rain, submerging nearby farmland. Datong and other places have largely been submerged. Fortunately, the inner embankments are high, thick, and sturdy. The local public security bureau led the security team, gathering hundreds of people, and prepared wooden piles, reed mats, and other materials to intensify the rescue efforts, preventing flooding. As for transportation, the impact has been even greater. On the Jiangnan Railway Company's Jin-Sun section, several sections of track between Xuancheng and Sunjiapu have been submerged, preventing traffic. Trains from Nanjing can only travel to Xuancheng via Wuhu. The Wutun Highway has been submerged near Wanzhi, and traffic has been interrupted. Buses have been suspended. It is reported that Xuancheng to Tunxi can still barely operate. The Huizhou-Hangzhou Highway has also been damaged, obstructing traffic. People's hearts in various places are now extremely uneasy. If it continues to rain for the next ten days, there is a great risk of complete submersion. (3rd)

Shandong: Unprecedented Crisis in the Cotton Industry; Severe Drought in Cotton Areas; Cotton Harvest This Year Is Almost Hopeless; More Than 100,000 Bales of Cotton Stockpiled in Jinan Are Stagnant 89

A dispatch from Jinan reports that cotton production accounts for a large proportion of Shandong's rural production. The annual output ranks first in the province's economic income. The banking industry in Jinan handles more than 10 million yuan in cotton mortgage loans each year, not including Qingdao. The relationship between the cotton industry and Shandong's economy can be imagined from this. The Department of Construction, in order to develop Shandong's economy, has devoted itself to the expansion of cotton and the improvement of the trial planting of American No. 36 Drilles cotton for several years, and has achieved great success. Therefore, this year, more than 2 million catties of cotton seeds will be distributed to various counties without charge to expand cotton fields in order to develop the cotton industry and relieve the rural economy. Unexpectedly, due to the impact of the domestic economic downturn, cotton in Jinan is stagnant and prices have fallen. The cotton accumulated on the market reached 130,000 to 140,000 bales. Although it has gradually become active in the past three to five days, there are still 110,000 to 120,000 bales that are stagnant and unsalable. Cotton merchants and flower shops are all crying out in pain. The most dangerous thing is the poor cotton harvest this year. This year, there has been a severe drought in various counties in Shandong. Although there has been rain in eastern and southern Shandong recently, there has been no rain in the cotton area of northern Shandong, including Linqing, Weihai, Gaotang, Tangyi, Xiajin, Qiuxian, Guanxian, Tangyi, Qingping, and Wucheng. Most of the cotton has not been planted, and the land is barren for thousands of miles. The harvest is hopeless, and the loss is no less than tens of millions of yuan, which has a huge impact on the rural economy of Shandong. Han Fuju, the chairman of the provincial government, has ordered the Department of Construction to quickly seek relief measures for the stagnant cotton and unplanted cotton fields, and set a deadline for implementation before the 15th of this month. Therefore, Zhang Honglie, the director of the Department of Construction, specially convened personnel related to the cotton industry throughout the province to Jinan to discuss everything. A meeting was held in the Department of Construction this morning (the 1st). Those who attended included Zhang Honglie, the director of the Department of Construction, Zhu Zhuxun, the chief of the First Section, Chen Shican, the technician, Wang Tengyun, the director of the Gaotang First Branch of the Shandong Cotton Talent Water Talent Miscellaneous Management Office, Zhu Zigui, the director of the Linqing Second Branch, Yang Dongtai, the director of the Zhangdian Third Branch, and the inspectors from Xiajin, Qiuxian, Guanxian, Tangyi, Qingping, Wucheng, and other six counties. Generally, the directors of the branches and the inspectors first reported on the cotton industry in their respective areas and whether the personnel in the office had any difficulties in their work. After the directors and inspectors finished their reports, it was noon, and the adjournment was announced. It was decided to continue the meeting tomorrow (the 2nd) to discuss everything.

Reporters interviewed Zhu Zigui, Wang Tengyun, and Yang Dongfeng separately about the situation in the cotton area of northern Shandong. According to them, northern Shandong is a cotton-producing area. This year, there was a severe drought without rain, and most of the cotton seeds have not been planted. The harvest is hopeless, and the loss is no less than tens of millions of yuan. The cotton-producing areas include Linqing, Gaotang, Xiajin, Qiuxian, Guanxian, Tangyi, Qingping, and Wucheng. Linqing County has more than 10,000 hectares of farmland, of which cotton fields account for 7,000 hectares. The average yield per mu is 80 catties of cotton, and the total output can reach 56 million catties of cotton. The price is 15 cents per catty, with a total value of 8.4 million yuan. Last year, due to the spring drought and poor harvest, each mu only yielded 60 catties, which was only 70% of the previous year. In addition, the price of cotton has fallen, and the loss has been not small. This year, not a drop of rain has fallen, and the cotton has not been planted. Even those who have watered and planted cotton only account for a very small number. The loss cannot be calculated. Gaotang County has more than 7,000 hectares of farmland, of which cotton fields account for more than 4,000 hectares. In previous years, each mu produced 80 to 90 catties of cotton, with a total output of about 32 million catties. At 15 cents per catty, the total value is 4.8 million yuan. Last year, due to the drought and poor harvest, only 60% to 70% was harvested. This year, the cotton planted only accounts for 60% to 70% of the 4,000 hectares. In other counties, the cotton was not planted due to the drought. As for Zhangdian, it is the place where cotton from Binzhou, Putai, and Lijin in northern Shandong is concentrated for export. The annual cotton concentrated passing through is within 200,000 dan. At present, flower shops in northern Shandong are mostly fleeing due to the low price of cotton, and the situation is extremely pitiful. (July 1st)

Zhang Ashui, a suspect in the robbery of Jin Juju's family in Xiaheng Township, Punan Seventh District, last month, residing in No. 11 Aizhuang, West Hutung, is highly suspected of being involved in the case. Incoming Document

Recent Brief Report from the Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Finance 102

— Wu Daye

Origin

The proposal to establish this bureau was made during the 33rd year of the Guangxu reign in the late Qing Dynasty. It was initially proposed by the Finance Department and subsequently discussed and approved by the Ministry of Revenue to establish regulations specifically for printing banknotes, with the aim of unifying currency and reclaiming economic rights. Therefore, the planning of the steel engraving department at that time was particularly detailed compared to other departments. Simultaneously, five American technicians were hired at great expense to be responsible for and teach this technology. However, the matter was in its initial stages, the scope was limited, and implementation was slow. It was not until June of the Xuantong reign that steel engraving printing could be done independently without foreign assistance. After the founding of the Republic of China, the bureau continued its previous work and further improved, achieving a large scale and clear organization. Since then, the equipment has become more complete, the business has become more developed, and the steel engraving technology has gained a reputation in East Asia.

From the establishment of this bureau to the present year, it has been twenty-seven years. The change of the national system and the turmoil of the political situation have had a significant impact on the bureau's affairs. The replacement of bureau directors has been almost annual. A business organization has been treated like a relay station for promotions. As a result, many have followed old habits and sought immediate benefits, while few have been forward-thinking and kept pace with the times. This description of the origin cannot help but evoke emotion.

(1) Establishment of the Bureau: In the 33rd year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, the Ministry of Revenue requested the establishment of a special bureau to print banknotes to unify currency and reclaim economic rights. The court approved the request, marking the beginning of this bureau. Since it was a new undertaking, many things were unclear. In addition to selecting a site in Baizhifang, first building a surrounding wall and several courtyards of old-style bungalows as preparation and office space, special personnel were appointed to investigate in the United States for guidance. Therefore, the overall construction design was drawn up by the American Miller & Brown Company. The civil engineering and construction were contracted to Japanese merchant Hua Sheng, and the mechanical installation was contracted to the American Lao Qichang foreign firm. All installations followed the regulations of the U.S. National Printing Bureau in Washington, D.C. In addition, three buildings in the east courtyard were built for staff accommodation and rest. Construction began in the summer of the Xuantong reign. During this time, an imperial decree was issued to merge the printing bureau established by the Ministry of Posts and Communications with this bureau. Simultaneously, three factories for letterpress printing were added and completed within a year. The main building project was not fully completed until the third year of the Republic of China, and the scale of the only printing bureau in the East was thus determined.

(2) Location of the Bureau: Located in Baizhifang inside Zhangyi Gate in Beijing, it occupies the extreme southwest corner of the city. It was the former site of the Qing Ministry of Works' gunpowder bureau. The rear and sides of the bureau wall are only dozens of steps away from the outer city wall. The total area of the bureau is about one million square feet, equivalent to more than 150 acres.

(3) Changes in the Bureau Name: It was initially named the Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Revenue. After the national system was updated, the Ministry of Revenue was renamed the Ministry of Finance, and the bureau was renamed the Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Finance. When the National Government moved south last year, the character "Ping" was added, becoming the Beiping Printing Bureau of the Ministry of Finance.

(4) Changes in the Bureau System: The head of this bureau was initially designated as a simplified position. In the Republic, it was changed to an appointed position. The person in charge was initially called the Director-General, with seated managers to assist. In the Republic, the Director-General was renamed the Bureau Director, and the titles of seated manager and co-manager were abolished. Underneath were the affairs and engineering departments, each governing six sections. In the Republic, the two departments were renamed the General Affairs and Engineering Sections, and the sections were renamed departments. In 1920, they were renamed the Business Office and Engineering Office, and the departments under their jurisdiction were renamed sections, which remains the case today.

(5) Advancement of Technology: When this bureau was first established, it was primarily responsible for printing banknotes of the Qing Bank, as well as stamps, revenue stamps, train tickets, public bonds, official documents, diplomas, contracts, grain receipts, salt and tea permits, broker licenses, and various official securities. At that time, regulations for the handover between the Post Office and the Printing Bureau were issued, and various regulations for distribution and anti-counterfeiting were formulated, which served as the foundation for printing in this bureau. At that time, regarding the engraving of steel plates and the printing of banknotes, since there was no such technology in the country, five engraving and steel plate experts were hired from the United States, and apprentices were recruited to train in engraving Qing banknotes.

(7) Revision of Bureau Regulations: In the Xuantong reign, when the preparation of this bureau was almost complete and work began, twenty-eight regulations were enacted to serve as guidelines for handling affairs. By 1916, the scale was complete, and the affairs became more complex, so they were added and amended and submitted to the ministry for record, but no special edition was published. In 1926, when Pu was in charge, revisions were added, and they were compiled into a book. It has been in use for over ten years, and with the passage of time and changes, it feels inappropriate. It is necessary to adopt the latest scientific management methods, carefully consider the advantages and disadvantages, and make detailed revisions in order to keep pace with the times and avoid falling behind. An order from the Ministry has been submitted for approval.

One-Year Review

(A) Review of the Previous Year's Situation: This bureau is a state-owned printing institution, established for twenty-seven years. Investments have exceeded millions, including the construction of factory buildings, the equipment of machinery, and the training of technical personnel, all of which have been described in the Origin chapter and will not be repeated here. However, due to repeated political changes and improper management, the bureau's debts have accumulated daily, and the situation is bleak. This was the situation reported last year on April and May. When Daye and others were ordered by the Ministry to take charge here, they investigated the accumulated losses of the bureau in the past and divided them into four categories: (1) Undelivered printed products: (A) A total of two batches of stamp tax tickets were owed, totaling six million sheets, with approximately over two hundred thousand yuan already collected. (B) Various valuable securities, with approximately over two hundred thousand yuan already collected in deposit money, and over one hundred thousand yuan designated for outstanding printing fees. The total is over seven hundred thousand yuan. (2) Bank loans: Loans from various banks that must be repaid immediately amount to over one million yuan. (3) Wage arrears: Unpaid salaries and wages for staff and workers total approximately seventy thousand yuan. (4) Losses on goods are no less than over one million yuan. At that time, in the midst of decline, there were such huge and urgent debts, and the unfavorable environment had reached its extreme. In addition, with the government moving south, all printed products were printed nearby. The headquarters of various banks moved to Shanghai, and there was less business in North China. This bureau worried that there were too many people and too few jobs, and it was not enough to cover expenses. Restructuring was not easy. However, the staff persisted, worked hard to reorganize, and set goals to be achieved. Although there has been no significant progress in one year, there have been gradual beginnings.

(B) Reorganization Situation in One Year: (1) Factory Reorganization: This bureau has thousands of craftsmen and apprentices with complex backgrounds. In the past, inspectors dared not seriously supervise, so the work was unorganized. At times, due to a lack of materials, some parts of the factory stopped working, while others rushing to produce finished products had to be processed separately. Half of the machines in each section were operating and half were stopped, and the losses in salaries and wages were huge, which was the main reason for previous losses. Recently, for the sake of reorganization, the various parts have been tightly and appropriately allocated. For all bureau workers, suitable ones are divided into two shifts, working in rotation, so that the printing machines are never idle and each worker has adequate rest. As for the materials used, they are ordered to be fully prepared in advance, so that all printed products can be completed on time, and wages can be saved. At the same time, the inspection section is ordered to seriously supervise. Over the past year, it has been quite effective. (2) Increasing Work Rate: Comparing and averaging the products of the factory in June, July, August, and September of the past year with those of previous years, the monthly output is approximately 180,000 yuan, an increase of one-third compared to previous years, which is the highest record of output rate in recent years for this bureau. (3) Reduction of Defective Products: In previous years, the defective products produced by the factory were worth about five percent. Recently, after ordering the engineering office to strictly supervise and implement rewards and punishments, it has now been reduced to thirteen percent, saving a lot of labor and materials throughout the year. (4) Reducing Fuel Consumption: Previously, all fuel was purchased from Kailuan Coal Mines. Because it was purchased in small quantities, the monthly cost was very high. Now it has been changed to bulk orders from Datong Kouquan Baoheng Company. Other scattered lump coal for furnaces is temporarily purchased from Kailuan. Beforehand, samples of Baoheng coal were ordered to be thoroughly tested by the responsible section, and the coal quality was excellent and the firepower was very strong. The actual burning results show that the monthly quantity required can be reduced by about 30% compared to Kailuan coal, while the price is the same. The full month can save at least more than one thousand yuan compared to using idle Kailuan coal. As for the number of furnaces opened each day, it is ordered by the engineering office to be determined temporarily according to the amount of printed products, in order to save fuel. Other measures to crack down on coal receiving staff and coal-burning workers are assigned to the section chiefs of the warehouse, machinery inspection, and other sections to be responsible for reporting at any time. (5) Establishment of a Material Purchasing Committee: Previously, the purchase of materials was all controlled by the purchasers themselves, and the examination was inevitably incomplete. There was no selection of the quality of the materials, and the prices were also expensive. Recently, a material purchasing committee has been established, jointly organized by the directors and section chiefs of various offices. All materials purchased are adopted using the method of open bidding, selecting those with the lowest price and excellent quality. It avoids being subject to the merchant's judgment and completely eliminates previous malpractices. Here are a few examples of the prices of materials used in the past and the prices of materials currently used, listed for comparison to examine the progress and decline of the past and present. (Table omitted) (6) Establishment of an Accounting Audit Committee: Previously, the revenue and expenditure of this bureau had never been carefully audited, so the annual budget and final accounts could not be prepared, strictly implemented. Now, an accounting audit committee has been established. All revenue and expenditure, as well as budgets and final accounts, must be submitted for review in order to ensure that no funds are wasted and that the accounts are accurate. (7) Formulation of Detailed Rules for Handling Affairs: Previously, each section only had temporary rules for handling affairs, which were not strictly followed and were mostly inconsistent with the actual situation, so there were often doubts when handling affairs. Rules were immediately drafted so that each section could follow them in handling affairs to facilitate progress. (8) Reducing Expenses: Previously, the amount of wages required for every 100,000 yuan of products was 29,300 yuan, and the price of materials required was approximately 60,000 to 70,000 yuan. Now, through efforts to save money, the amount of wages required for every 100,000 yuan of products is 22,600 yuan, which is actually a reduction of more than 6,000 yuan compared to the past, and the price of materials required is approximately 50,000 yuan, which is actually a reduction of more than 10,000 yuan to over 10,000 yuan compared to the past. (9) Establishment of an Art Research Association: The printed products of this bureau have not been very well received by society in terms of art. As a result, major banks order banknotes from abroad. This is not only a shortcoming of steel plate engraving in the printing bureau, but also the biggest leak in our country. Now, an art research association has been established to mutually observe and earnestly improve what can be imitated and what can be adopted in the new trends of modern work and the excellent technology of Europe and the United States. We must promote the elimination of the old and bring forth the new in order to expand business and prevent the outflow of economic rights. The progress that has been made includes various fine lines and multi-color overprinting to prevent counterfeiting. The items printed in recent months seem to have new and innovative contributions. (10) Making Up for Accumulated Losses: Previously, 600,000 stamp tax tickets were owed, with a total price of approximately 340,000 yuan. Various valuable securities, with approximately 300,000 yuan already collected in deposit money. Loans from various banks that must be repaid immediately amount to over 600,000 yuan. Unpaid salaries and wages for staff and workers total approximately 70,000 yuan. Overdue payments for goods amount to over 100,000 yuan. The total is over one million yuan. Now, within one year, the current director has repaid approximately 90,000 yuan in principal and interest to the Central Bank, China Bank, Jin Cheng Bank, and Hebei Bank on behalf of the previous director, as well as other scattered debts, paid 50,000 yuan in arrears of salaries and wages, and paid 150,000 yuan for printing costs in various places, with the accumulated losses being made up for being approximately over 500,000 yuan. If the business develops in the future and all domestic bank banknotes are printed by this bureau, then the previous debts can be gradually paid off.

The difference between steel engraving printing and other printing. The essential elements for the production of printed matter rely entirely on the printing surface, equipment, and ink. Each printing surface has its own machine and ink to match it. And each printing surface is divided into various procedures such as engraving and plating. Engraving is the process by which the original plate is made. Both steel engraving and ordinary engraving are different and more difficult. The engraving methods are roughly divided into three types: (1) using thick and thin horizontal lines to distinguish between yin and yang, (2) using thick and thin warp and weft lines to distinguish between yin and yang, and (3) adding dots to vary the density to distinguish between yin and yang. Please try examining the banknotes and stamps of various countries with a microscope, and you will be able to see the difference. However, it is impossible to see the mystery with the naked eye. The most famous steel engraving artist in the past was an American named Haichu. This bureau once hired him as a professor at a high cost of 1,500 US dollars per month, and he stayed in the bureau for five years. This person is now deceased. Plating is the process of engraving the size of the original plate on the steel shaft with large and small patterns and the size of the large plate, which is more important work and has special machines for it. Nowadays, the most important printed products used in various countries around the world are bank banknotes and tax stamps. However, countries have different habits for important printed products, so the printing surfaces used are also different. For example, the United States mostly combines steel intaglio and copper relief printing. In the old Russian era, the five-color patterns printed on the ruble notes were exquisite and unparalleled in the world. European, American, and countries all imitated them, but they never achieved the same level of exquisiteness because the machines they used have not been made public to the world. This proves that the three types of printing, printing surface, machine, and ink, are equally important and indispensable. We will not discuss the machine and ink for now. Let's first talk about the types, properties, and uses of the printing surface. The printing surface has three types: relief, planographic, and intaglio. Relief prints are those where the text and patterns are raised above the surface of the printing surface, such as ordinary lead plates and woodblocks. Planographic prints are those where the text and patterns are level with the printing surface. When making the printing surface, another kind of chemical is used to make the printing surface have the effect of attracting and repelling ink, such as today's lithographic and rubber printing surfaces. Intaglio prints are those where the text and patterns are recessed below the surface of the printing surface, which is the opposite of relief prints. When printing, the ink absorbed by the paper from this depression forms the text, which is today's steel printing surface. The reason why steel is used for intaglio prints is that it is strong, tough, and dense, while copper is slightly inferior to steel. Therefore, the text and patterns engraved on a copper printing surface cannot be as deep and fine as those on a steel printing surface. If you engrave fine and dense lines, you can clearly distinguish them on a steel printing surface, but you cannot distinguish them on a copper printing surface. Sometimes two lines may even become one line because the material is not as dense as steel. The same is true for width and depth. In the engraving of landscape patterns, the most important thing is the contrast of light and dark, which depends on the depth of the lines. The ability of the lines to distinguish between depth depends on the density of the printing surface material. Steel printing surfaces are able to engrave deeply because of their fine and dense material, while copper is not. In terms of printing, copper is stronger than copper. If a copper printing surface is printed too many times, the engraved patterns will become blurred and unrecognizable, and even the printing surface will be polished and the patterns will disappear. Steel printing surfaces do not easily have this phenomenon because of their strong material. Moreover, the printing surface is definitely not something that can be used by a single block, so there are various procedures such as the original printing surface. Steel printing surfaces can be used to engrave shafts with original printing surfaces, which are cylindrical rollers. Then, the engraved shaft is used to plate large copper printing surfaces or six-open or eight-open printing surfaces, each with the same patterns. If it is a copper printing surface, the material is extremely soft. After the original printing surface is made, it cannot be mounted on a shaft. What it relies on is photography or wax plating electroplating. The large printing surfaces plated with photography and wax plating can also be divided into several parts, but their patterns must not be accurate. Furthermore, steel printing surfaces use specially made soft steel printing surfaces for engraving and plating. After the printing surface is made, it is hardened by fire, making it harder than normal. The machines and operations for hardening with fire are difficult to describe in a few words. Copper printing surfaces cannot be hardened by smelting, but only steel has this effect. After the printing surface is smelted and hardened, it can withstand the heavy pressure of the printing machine, but copper printing surfaces cannot withstand heavy pressure. If the printing surface is pressed, the patterns will not change easily. If it is not pressed, the patterns will change easily. Therefore, countries like China and the United States use steel intaglio printing for the most important banknotes and tax stamps, and are unwilling to use copper intaglio printing because this is the key. Nowadays, printing technology is extremely developed, and the distinction between copper printing surfaces and steel printing surfaces is not very clear to the general public, so I will briefly describe it without being too tedious.

notes, and pointing to the printing of stamps, tax tickets and various steel plates. By the third and fourth years of the Republic, the apprentices had made great progress and were gradually able to come up with their own ideas. In 1916, another class of apprentices was added to continue learning. Afterwards, only one foreign technician, Gellan, was retained to provide advice and consultation. In 1927, Gellan also terminated his contract and left. Since then, the steel plate work of this bureau has been entirely made by Chinese people and no longer relies on foreigners. All the products are no less inferior to those made in Europe and the United States. They have won the best award certificates and medals in various international product competitions in Tsintao.

(6) Purchase of Machines: Once the proposal to establish this bureau was decided, personnel were first sent to the United States to purchase and transport all the machines. At the same time, the building was built, and the machines were installed and completed. Although there were subsequent additions, they were small-scale or partial machine parts, and no major construction was added. Notable events include receiving 900,000 jin of ingots from the Baoquan Bureau in the third year of Xuantong to add to the casting of lead type. In 1912, paper cutting machines, lead printing machines, lithographic printing machines, punching machines, and color lithographic printing machines were added. In 1915, lead printing machines from the first library branch were purchased, and American zinc plate printing machines, electroplating machines, and plating machines were ordered, and zinc plate printing machines were first used. In 1921, telephone switchboards were added. In 1922, technician Shen Yongbin successfully researched multi-color printing and set up multi-color machines, which was the beginning of multi-color printing for this bureau.

Letter 103

To the reporter, I have recently read a news item in your newspaper on May 16 entitled "Pointing to the Good as Prostitutes and Inciting a Strike." After investigation, many of the facts do not match the truth. Banning prostitution and gambling is the responsibility of the Public Security Bureau. Inciting a strike on this pretext and gathering crowds inside the Public Security Bureau to carry out coercion is a crime under Articles 142 and 143 of the Criminal Law. This bureau is now investigating the instigators and sending them to the county for legal action in order to warn the stubborn and deter the prestige. As for destroying the sound waves, it was originally the section chief of the second section of this bureau. Because the branch director Zhang Jue asked for a week's leave, Yin was temporarily appointed as a substitute. He has now been transferred back to his original position and there is no matter of dismissal or investigation. I am hereby informing you, hoping that you will correct it accordingly. Sincerely, the editor-in-chief of the Central Daily News, the Public Security Bureau of Haimen County, July 1st.

Shipping Fees for Goods to the United States Will Increase; To be Implemented from August 1st 106

The shipping of goods from Shanghai to the United States is divided into two routes: the Pacific Line and the New York Line. The shipping fees for each route are determined by the Shipping Fee Conference composed of various foreign shipping companies. All member companies that join the conference must charge according to the fixed rate and are not allowed to increase or decrease the fees without authorization. Recently, due to the relationship between gold prices, the exchange rate has changed compared to before, and the shipping rates set for each route are mostly based on US dollars, which is not very cost-effective when converted into Shanghai silver dollars. Therefore, various shipping companies, such as Dollar, Changxing, Nippon Yusen, Osaka, Blue Funnel, Jardine, and Pacific, sent representatives to a meeting to increase the shipping fees for goods on each route, otherwise the exchange rate would be too low. After discussion, the representatives of the companies decided that the shipping prices for goods on both the Pacific Line and the New York Line will be increased uniformly from August 1st, by approximately one to three US dollars per ton. All goods must be fully increased. The amount to be increased is currently being proposed, and the amount of the increase will be determined based on whether the goods are essential or secondary.

World Bank Ceases Operations, Has Absolutely No Connection with World Book Company 111

According to the New Voice News Agency, the World Bank at 400 Fuzhou Road was established on January 5, 1930, and registered with the government on April 2, 1931, with a capital of 200,000 national currency units. It has a history of six years. It engages in both commercial and savings operations, and its lending activities have been relatively stable. Recently, due to the economic downturn, loan repayments have been difficult to collect, causing a temporary inability to circulate funds. The bank's board of directors decided to temporarily cease operations yesterday morning. It has been found that the bank currently has savings deposits of approximately 500,000 units, and the government bonds deposited with the Central Bank are valued at approximately 130,000 to 140,000 units at current market prices. The assets are sufficient to cover the liabilities, so there should be no problem for depositors to withdraw their savings in the future. The manager of the bank was originally Xie Yuru, but since Mr. Xie left office due to personal reasons, the deputy manager has been temporarily acting as manager.

Entrusted Public Notice of Temporary Suspension of Business: Jiang Yiping, Lawyer, and Jiang Wanping, Accountant, Represent the World Commercial Savings Bank in Announcing the Temporary Suspension of Business: "It is now stated by the Board of Directors of the World Commercial Savings Bank that due to the economic downturn and the severe credit crunch, the bank is temporarily unable to circulate funds. The Board of Directors has resolved to temporarily suspend business from today and to convene an emergency shareholders' meeting to discuss the aftermath. All of the bank's books and important documents, etc., have been entrusted to your esteemed lawyers and accountants for temporary safekeeping, and you are requested to issue a public notice on behalf of the bank after the shareholders' meeting decides on a plan, etc." Based on this, we hereby issue a public notice on behalf of the bank, dated July 4, 1935.

World Book Company Has Absolutely No Connection: The World Book Company was established in 1921 as a limited liability company, initiated by Shen Zhifang and others, with a capital of 25,000. As of now, the total capital has increased to one million. The current directors are Li Shizeng, Chu Minyi, Du Chongyuan, Du Yuesheng, Cui Zhuxi, Wang Yiting, Qian Xinzhi, Li Shuhua, Lu Shenliang, Wu Yunqi, Chen Hexian, Shen Zhifang, Zhang Jingjiang, Jin Zhaoyan, and Lu Gaoyi. The current supervisors are Wu Zhihui, Li Linyu, and Qi Yunqing. The chairman of the board is Zhang Jingjiang, the supervisor is Shen Zhifang, and the general manager is Lu Gaoyi. The World Book Company has absolutely no connection with the World Commercial Savings Bank. Therefore, the temporary suspension of business of the World Bank will not have the slightest impact on the World Book Company.

Sino-French Savings Society Terminates Prize-Linked Savings, Temporarily Suspends Collection and Transfers to the Central Trust Bureau, Resumption of Business After Transfer is Completed, Depositors Suffer No Loss 112

The Sino-French Savings Society was established in early August 1918 as a joint venture between China and France, registered with the French Consulate in Tianjin and the Chinese government. In 1926, it was reorganized into a Chinese limited liability company, and all French shares were repurchased. In 1934, it applied to the Ministry of Finance to establish ordinary savings operations, with a capital of 450,000 national currency units. The head office was located in Beiping, and branch offices were established in Shanghai, Hangzhou, Shantou, Tianjin, Nanjing, Fuzhou, Hankou, Guangzhou, Xiamen, Anqing, Changsha, and other places. Since the National Government promulgated the Savings Bank Law, which prohibited prize-linked savings, the Society immediately followed the instructions of the Ministry of Finance to terminate prize-linked savings and, with the approval of the Ministry of Finance, transferred the depositors to ordinary savings.

Ministry of Finance Instruction: The Society received Qian Zi No. 10 from the Ministry of Finance, stating: "A document is submitted to the effect that, in order to comply with laws and regulations, the Savings Society is voluntarily terminating its savings operations and urgently needs cash for application purposes, and proposing solutions to be reviewed and instructed on. The document is received and understood. According to the report, the Society is voluntarily terminating its operations and is experiencing difficulties in circulating funds, which is a factual situation. The request to hand over all assets and liabilities of Parts A and B of the Society to the Central Trust Bureau for handling is hereby approved. You should immediately contact the Central Bank Trust Bureau to complete the handover procedures. The directors, supervisors, and managers of the Society can only be relieved of their responsibilities after the Trust Bureau has clarified the assets and liabilities and the assets are sufficient to offset the debts. In addition to sending a letter to the Central Bank for their information, you should comply accordingly. This is the instruction."

Public Notice of Transfer: The Society's head office in Beiping and all branch offices temporarily suspended all collection and payment activities from yesterday to expedite the transfer. The Shanghai branch of the Society at 175 Guangdong Road in this city posted a public notice of temporary suspension of collection and payment at its entrance yesterday morning, stating: "This Society has recently received Order No. 10 from the Ministry of Finance, instructing that all assets and liabilities of Parts A and B of this Society be handed over to the Trust Bureau of the Central Bank for takeover. We will certainly comply with the order and expedite the handover procedures. During this period of handover, collection and payment activities will be temporarily suspended in order to facilitate the Central Bank's takeover and continued operation as soon as possible. This is hereby announced."

Yesterday's Takeover: The Central Bank specially dispatched Zhang Nachuan, Chen Zhongsheng, Wang Yixuan, and three others at 10:00 AM yesterday to meet with Wu Wu Da, the manager of the Shanghai branch of the Sino-French Savings Society, to negotiate the handover procedures. It is reported that the Sino-French Savings Society temporarily suspended collection and payment activities to the public yesterday, but continued to work internally to expedite the closing of accounts in order to facilitate the transfer. At 2:00 PM yesterday, Chen Zhongsheng and others brought an official letter from the Trust Bureau of the Central Bank to the Sino-French Savings Society to conduct a formal takeover. It is estimated that the entire assets, etc., can be taken over completely today. After the Central Bank Trust Bureau completes its review, the business will revert to the Trust Bureau. It is understood that the Society has decided to transfer all assets and liabilities of the two types of savings to the Central Bank Trust Bureau and then proceed with the liquidation. After the Trust Bureau completes its review, the Central Bank Trust Bureau will take over, so depositors will not suffer any losses, and there will be no impact on Shanghai's financial market.

Ruilong Company Ceases Operations 113

According to the New Voice News Agency, Ruilong Yuangi Paint Company, located at 8 Ning Shao Lane, Jiangxi Road, has a long history and is known for its reliability. It has ceased operations a few days ago due to the impact of advances to Hengsheng Public Silk Factory and owes more than one million yuan. The details are as follows:

Announcement of Suspension of Business

Ruilong Yuangi Company was reorganized from Qian Yuanlai and has been in operation for 33 years since its inception, with a total history of more than 80 years. It was established as a joint venture by Bei Jian Sheng and others, and its scope was extensive, enjoying a good reputation in the paint industry. It made huge profits during the European War. Now, Bei Runsheng, Zhao Yuting, and Zhao Jizhai have withdrawn their shares, and the company has been jointly operated by He Puxian and Wang Yunfu. Recently, due to the gradual decline of the paint industry, the company has been incurring losses annually. The shareholders of the company, He Pu and Wang Yunfu, also operate Hengsheng Public Silk Store, which specializes in Shandong yellow silk. Recently, due to the sharp drop in silk prices, the company has continuously made advances totaling more than 600,000 yuan. As a result, the company was unable to sustain itself and had to declare bankruptcy at the end of last month during the bank's semi-annual closing period.

Total Debt

The amount of Ruilong's debt is as follows: (1) Long-term loans: Yu Kang 10,000, Sino-American 20,000, Ningji 24,000, Hengli 14,000, Xieji 56,000, Xinjiji 10,000, Yuji 60,000, Yongqing 60,000, Jukang 5,000, Yuanji 8,000, Hengfu 30,000, Jianzhong 5,000, Dunyu 5,000, Binfeng 7,000, Shanghai 10,000, Qingtai 15,000, Xinyu 20,000, Ruifu 5,000; (2) Current accounts: Yu Kang 43,400, Quangong 25,300, China 20,800, Hengli 26,800, Yufeng 21,800, Zhiyu 26,100, Jiangzhe 9,800, Ruichang 80,200, Tongrun 5,900, Zhenkang 4,100, Dakang 2,100, Dunyu 7,200, Baofeng 8,800, Shanghai 19,000, Huizhong 1,700, Xinyu 19,500; (3) Pledged loans: Hengli 14,000, Ruichang 10,000, Baofeng 38,000. Deposits total 320,000 yuan. The total is more than 1,060,000 yuan.

Negotiating Discounts

The assets of Ruilong, as learned by a reporter from the New Voice News Agency, are as follows: (1) Inventory of paints, etc., approximately 30,000 yuan; (2) Indigo oil, approximately 60,000 yuan; (3) Customer accounts, approximately 10,000 yuan; (4) Advances to Hengsheng Public, approximately 670,000 yuan; (5) Dadong Real Estate, approximately 100,000 yuan. The total is approximately 870,000 yuan. However, it is difficult to collect the above items. Compared with the total liabilities, there is a shortage of approximately 200,000 yuan. Ruilong Yuangi Paint Company has entrusted a well-known businessman to negotiate debt discounts with various creditors, and negotiations are currently underway. No specific solutions have been decided yet.

A supplementary code book is attached to the association. Therefore, we are forwarding the facts and attaching a sample of the supplementary code book, requesting that you check, one, and give a verification certificate, etc. It was delivered to the association, and it was found that the supplementary code book sent was copied from the original general clearing account for the convenience of the manager's audit. It does not create any rights or obligations to the outside world. It is not the nature of the voucher referred to in Article 1 of the Provisional Regulations on Stamp Duty. Even the various trades mentioned in Article 2 of the regulations refer to the account books established by shops. Personal excerpts for reference when performing duties should not be included. We hereby submit the same sample to your department for verification and request that you instruct and implement it. This is for public service. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce respectfully bows to Jiang."

The required construction costs were also allocated by the Bureau from the wharf and berthing fees. Wharf No. 13, planned by the Bureau, is a full steel floating wharf with a length of 55 meters, a width of 7.32 meters, and a height of 2.13 meters, with two floating bridges, each with a length of 12.24 meters and a width of 4.875 meters. Wharf No. 18 is a full steel floating wharf with a length of 45.72 meters, a width of 6.1 meters, and a height of 1.83 meters, with a floating bridge with a length of 12.32 meters and a width of 4.875 meters. This year, the construction project was openly tendered in January and won by the Huada Iron Works and the Jiangnan Shipyard, respectively. The construction project is now reported to be completed and installed. On June 25, the Municipal Government dispatched personnel to the site along with the Municipal Bureau of Public Works for formal inspection and acceptance. Wharf No. 13 is leased by the Sanbei Company, while Wharf No. 18 is a public wharf.

Municipal Government Petitions for Strict Investigation of Rumor-Mongering to Stabilize Public Sentiment and Maintain Market Stability 125

Central News Agency, Nanjing, 4th: The Shanghai Municipal Government stated that Shanghai is the financial center of China, and recently, there have been unscrupulous people deliberately spreading rumors in an attempt to confuse public sentiment and profit from it. Kong Xiangxi Talks About the Good Progress of President Wang's Treatment and the Authorities' Strict Prevention of the Yangtze River Flooding 126

According to the Central News Agency, Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi, accompanied by Fu Rulin and others, arrived in Shanghai from Beijing on the night express yesterday morning. After getting off the train, he returned to his private residence on West End Road and met with reporters from various newspapers. According to him, President Wang's fever has gradually subsided, and his treatment is progressing well. As for the rising water level of the Yangtze River, the government has ordered Fu Rulin, Chairman of the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission, and Mao Yisheng, Director of the Water Conservancy Department of the Economic Committee, to supervise the technical personnel and strictly prevent flooding. The details are as follows:

President Wang's Treatment is Progressing Well: President Wang's old illness recurred, so he requested leave to come to Shanghai for diagnosis and treatment at the Noel Hospital. Mr. Wang is suffering from both diabetes and liver disease, and his bile ducts are blocked by stones, causing inflammation in the bile ducts. While I was in Beijing, I received a telegram from President Wang, stating that his fever had gradually subsided and that his treatment was progressing well. I expect that he will recover in the short term. I plan to visit him in the afternoon.

Kong Temporarily Replaces Wang in Political Affairs: During Mr. Jiang's leave, all affairs of the Executive Yuan will be temporarily handled by me. As for the affairs of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, Vice Ministers Xu Tan and Tang Youren will be responsible for handling them under the supervision of President Wang. As for the 13th Standing Committee Meeting of the National Economic Committee and other committees, it was originally scheduled to be held in Beijing at the beginning of the month, but it has been postponed due to Mr. Wang's illness. Mr. Kong also said that the Chahar incident has been completely resolved.

Increased Prevention of Yangtze River Flooding: Mr. Kong continued, "Regarding the prevention of the rising water level of the Yangtze River, the government authorities are paying close attention to it due to the recent continuous heavy rains and the rising water level in various sections of the Yangtze River. For precautionary purposes, Fu Rulin, Chairman of the Yangtze River Water Conservancy Commission, and Mao Yisheng, Director of the Water Conservancy Department of the National Economic Committee, have been strictly ordered to supervise all technical personnel and the section chiefs of various sections of the Yangtze River to carry out prevention work, so as not to cause flooding. According to the observation of general hydrologists, although the water level of the Yangtze River is rising, if it is sunny and there is no rain in the coming days, the river water can recede and will not reach the shore."

Standing Committee Meeting of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce Approves the Outline of the Industrial and Commercial Revitalization Association 127

Appointed Chen Guangfu, Wang Zhishen, and 50 others as committee members; Zhang Naiqi, Pan Yangyao, Luo Qinghua, and others as directors of various groups; and recommended Wang Yansong and Yan Esheng as principals of the Commercial Middle School.

Since the Sixth General Meeting of Members of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce resolved to organize an Industrial and Commercial Revitalization Committee, establish a Commercial Middle School, and expand supplementary education to train fundamental talents for commercial revitalization, the Joint Executive and Supervisory Committee nominated the Director of the Revitalization Committee, and the Standing Committee nominated 15 members of the Commercial Middle School Board of Directors, decided on a commercial night school, and launched a summer training program. All these initiatives are progressing very actively. Yesterday at 2:00 PM, another Standing Committee meeting was held to discuss the organizational outline of the Revitalization Committee and the candidates for committee membership. The attendees included Wang Yansong, Director of the Revitalization Committee; Yu Zuoting, Chairman of the Committee; Standing Committee members Xu Jilong, Jin Runxiang, Chen Zheqing, Ke Ganchen; Pan Xusheng, Director of the General Affairs Section; Ma Shaoquan, Director of the Commercial Affairs Section; Zheng Zenan, Director of the Finance Section; and Secretary Zhu Boyuan. Yu Zuoting, Chairman, immediately initiated the discussion on,

Organizational Outline of the Revitalization Association

The following articles were passed one by one: (1) This association is based on the Sixth General Meeting of Members of the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce. This association shall have one Director, who shall be hired by the Executive Committee. There shall be no fixed number of committee members, who shall be hired by the Director in consultation with the Standing Committee. (3) At meetings of this association, the Director shall serve as Chairman. (4) Decisions at meetings of this association shall require the consent of more than half of the committee members present. In case of a tie, the Chairman shall have the deciding vote. (5) This association shall have one Executive Director, who shall be hired by this association and shall carry out the Director's instructions in handling various affairs of this association. (6) This association shall temporarily establish four groups: General Affairs, Investigation, Statistics, and Training. Each group shall have one Director, one Deputy Director, and several members, who shall be transferred from the staff of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. When necessary, they may also be appointed by this association. (7) This association may establish subcommittees for research as needed. (8) This outline shall be implemented after being approved by the Executive Committee of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and the same shall apply to amendments.

Recommendation of Committee Members and Directors

Next, the case of the candidate list for committee membership was discussed. It was decided that, in addition to the consultant members of the Chamber of Commerce, Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaoji, Wang Yansong, Qin Runqing, Bei Songsun, and the 22 members of the Executive and Supervisory Committee as ex officio members, and Wang Yansong as Director, the following 25 individuals would also be appointed as committee members: Chen Guangfu, Wang Zhishen, Pan Xulun, Xu Yongzuo, Zhang Naiqi, Pan Yangyao, Li Wenjie, Xi Yushu, Jin Zongcheng, Jin Guomai, Zhu Yinong, Yang Yinpu, Huang Renzhi, Pan Mingzhi, Gao Shiheng, Rong Jingxiu, Xu Xiaochu, Xiang Kangyuan, Wang Yunwu, Gu Zhuanyi, Xu Guanqun, Mei Zhezhi, Fang Yixian, Guo Shun, Xu Caichen, etc. At the same time, Yan Esheng was recommended as Director of the General Affairs Group, Ren Jinpin as Deputy Director, Xi Yushu as Director of the Investigation Group, Xu Xiaochu as Deputy Director, Zhang Naiqi as Director of the Statistics Group, Luo Qinghua as Director of the Training Group, and Pan Yangyao as Deputy Director. The position of Executive Director will be concurrently held by Ren Jinpin. After the Standing Committee meeting,
