Free Talk

On Elegance 220

— Yao Xueyin

Elegance is a good adjective in both Chinese life and art. Its meaning is leisure, purity, and etherealness. We don't have a complete dictionary to find out exactly when it was used as a representative of a beautiful concept, but generally speaking, it was enthusiastically advocated and worshiped starting in the Wei and Jin dynasties. At that time, it was enough to resist the high pressure of rituals and powerful ministers, and it had the same meaning as pure conversation. Although pure conversation was most influenced by Lao Tzu and Zhuangzi, elegance was due to the use of Five Stone Powder. However, He Yan, the ancestor of pure conversation, was also the first to use Five Stone Powder, which clearly tells us the relationship between the two.

According to Mr. Lu Xun's research, Five Stone Powder was almost equivalent to opium in the late Qing Dynasty and became a very common addiction. After taking Five Stone Powder, one had to eat cold food, drink hot wine, and bathe in cold water and go for a walk. People who took Five Stone Powder did not wear shoes but sandals because their skin was easily broken. They wore loose clothing because they felt hot. As for whether people who took Five Stone Powder became thin, Mr. Lu Xun did not specify, but I think they would not be fat. Once a person becomes thin, wears loose clothing, and does not participate in physical labor, he naturally becomes elegant. Therefore, when we mention the word "elegance," we cannot help but associate it with hermits, poets, and figures from the Wei and Jin dynasties. Mr. Lu Xun said that those who took Five Stone Powder during the Wei and Jin dynasties were not poor. In fact, not only were they not poor, but even merchants were not worthy of it. Because the past culture was the culture of feudal landlords, pot-bellied merchants were regarded as vulgar things. Only the feudal landlord class, especially the literati from this class, talked about elegance.

Elegance not only appeared in history in a posture of resistance, but was also directly related to feudal status concepts and closely combined with the material life of feudal landlords. In the feudal era, the life of the landlord class was leisurely, and participating in physical labor was considered a loss of status. For example, growing long fingernails, foot binding for men, and wearing long gowns were all ways to show that they were leisurely and had status. Life determined customs, and customs influenced the concept of beauty. Therefore, at that time, all leisurely hobbies, such as tasting tea, raising birds, composing poems, and playing the qin, chess, calligraphy, and painting, became elegant. In painting, landscape paintings were particularly developed and valued, which expressed people's longing for an elegant life. Landscape paintings were an expansion of the landlord class's desire for leisure, hoping to get rid of the hustle and bustle of the world and live in the mountains and forests with the clear breeze and bright moon. They also observed things from their own perspective. Bamboo became a representative of elegance, and the pitiful fishermen and woodcutters were also beautiful subjects for poems and paintings.

In music, we see the special popularity of Qingchang and Xiao board in history. Chinese music takes mellowness and purity as its orthodox style. On the one hand, it is due to the beautiful relationship between the lives of landlords and literati, and on the other hand, it cannot be unaffected by the concept of loving elegance. The story of the Tang Dynasty people singing seven-character quatrains and painting on the walls of flag pavilions is eternally fascinating. As for mentioning the Song Dynasty people singing poems, we immediately think of poets carrying prostitutes on boats on moonlit nights, and the scene of "Little Red singing softly and me playing the xiao." After the Song Dynasty, Sanqu replaced the status of Ci. However, it is also based on mellowness and purity, mostly quiet and delicate tunes. There are no gongs and drums or dialogue when singing, so it is also called Qingqu. Yuan Zhonglang, who paid the most attention to elegance, said in "A Record of Tiger Hill": "By late at night, the Xiao board was no longer used. When one person took the stage, the audience held their breath, and the sound was like a fine hair, echoing through the clouds." How pure and elegant this is!

Elegance is expressed in literature as a combination of light and spiritual styles. Originally, the two were interrelated and difficult to separate. In history, both had rebellious significance. Tao Yuanming and Yuan Zhonglang were both literary rebels of their time. In the era of Tao Yuanming, court literati led literature to a dead end, with only a gorgeous shell and no soul. In the era of Yuan Zhonglang, the trend of imitating the ancients was particularly prevalent, and literati forgot that there was still a self when writing. Therefore, Tao Yuanming and Yuan Zhonglang both tried their best to pursue nature. There are two kinds of nature: one is the nature of scenery, and the other is the nature of human nature. Leaning towards the nature of scenery, one tends to express the love of landscapes and pastoral gardens. Leaning towards the nature of human nature, one opposes imitation of the ancients and meaningless rules. Combining the two is the liberation from the shackles of reality and the ultimate in elegance.

However, although elegance is a good noun, we cannot forget that it is a vestige of the feudal era, and its supporters are the feudal landlord class and the literati from this class. The social conditions that adapt to it have now collapsed, and if we advocate it again, we will not get the sympathy of most people.

Tokyo Correspondence 221

— Luo Zhi

The Pure Novel Theory and Veritable Record Literature Theory in the Japanese Literary World

The change in social life influences changes in literature; this is a natural axiom. Now in Japan, due to the changing currents of social life, endless replacements are also occurring in the literary world. The topic of early spring—Activism—is now becoming a thing of people's memories. However, just as summer comes to succeed spring, old topics in the literary world are being replaced by new ones. These new topics we can point to are the so-called "Pure Novel Theory" and "Veritable Record Literature Theory." The former was first advocated by Riichi Yokomitsu, and the latter by Sanji Kisaki. A separate account is given below:

Pure Novel Theory

The "Pure Novel Theory" is essentially something with the character of a literary methodology, so since Riichi Yokomitsu published his essay "Pure Novel Theory" in the April issue of "Kaizo," it caused a great commotion. All the writers and critics commented on it from various angles. For example, Keiyama Moriyama, in elucidating the accidental and inevitable nature of literature, severely criticized Riichi Yokomitsu's opinions on accidentality and inevitability. Similarly, Mineo Teraoka, standing on the commonality of literature, pointed out the non-commonality of the Pure Novel Theory. According to Riichi Yokomitsu himself, the essence of the Pure Novel Theory is to harmonize and integrate the current popular novels and pure literature, creating a grand romantic world like that of Dostoevsky or Balzac. It is to break away from the narrow and limited diary confession literature of the past and further create the kind of novel that the 19th century left behind—that is, fiction in the true sense, yet permeated with literary truth, a pure novel with higher artistic creation. Therefore, it addresses issues such as "commonality and purity," "accidentality and inevitability," and "long novels and short novels." At the same time, it also proposes the issue of the "fourth-person" expression method. In this view, the Pure Novel Theory seems to be solely exploring literary techniques, but in general understanding, Yokomitsu's pursuit of these expressive techniques also has something he wants to express, which makes him do so, that is, it also has a certain content. So what is he trying to express? This is the "self-consciousness" that dominates people's inner selves. So-called self-consciousness is people's method of dealing with real life and their desires. This kind of thing is expressed a lot in modern Japanese literature. Some combine it with the direction of history to whip themselves, trying to align themselves with objective reality. However, Yokomitsu's so-called self-consciousness is not like that. His self-consciousness is contemplative; it is a quest for one's inner self, detached from objective reality. It lacks any subjective meaning. Please see what he says through the character of Kyunai Yamashita in his novel "Crest."

"A so-called free person is someone who has a broad and unfettered spirit that allows them to independently and coolly observe their own emotions and thoughts. Mr. Karigane is an enemy to me, but only because he is an enemy, his behavior strongly teaches me what this spirit of freedom is…!"

This clearly expresses that Kyunai Yamashita's broad and unfettered spirit—self-consciousness—cannot become a strong spirit of freedom that whips and transforms oneself unless it can independently observe from the object in a cool manner.

Therefore, in order to express this internal self-awareness, Yokomitsu proposed the issue of the fourth person in the novel and also hoped for long novels because "doing it this way…the writer can only die with short stories" (Yokomitsu's words). And because the movement of this white consciousness is very accidental, he hopes to introduce the accidentality of popular literature. Thus, the so-called Pure Novel Theory is created.

The above is a general explanation of the Pure Novel, its origin, and content. Now let's move on to the second issue.

Veritable Record Literature Theory

The advocacy of veritable record literature has a long history, brewing since last November, but it was not until recently that Sanji Kisaki published an essay, "The Proposition of Veritable Record Literature," in the May issue of "Bungei," that it became an issue in the literary world. This issue was not as lively as the previous one. Currently, only Nao Tokunaga is participating in this discussion. Veritable record literature is healthy popular literature. Please see what Sanji Kisaki says:

"Digging out the history buried by falsehoods, connecting its direction of movement to our present from a realistic perspective and depicting this. Such interesting popular literature must be written to be effective in opening the eyes of the masses… It follows a parallel line with realistic literature that clearly teaches the realistic significance left by history. This is a kind wish of literary scholars who mobilize a part of the function of literature and want to help the improvement of popular culture… Veritable record literature is still a creation. But it must be produced as popular literature. In this way, it cannot be absurd and unfounded. It must be a very interesting novel that extracts the realistic meaning from the subject matter… This can never become the highest artistic literature of the present. Therefore, from the standpoint of artistic literature, this kind of popular literature can be called cultural reading material that enlightens the lives of the masses—that is, 'public reading material.'"

This is almost all of Sanji Kisaki's theory of veritable record literature. That is, using historical subject matter, using new perspectives, to create a new type of popular literature—literature with lower artistic qualities. Regarding the basis for Kisaki's advocacy of this veritable record literature, he himself also stated:

"For example, what use is it to say to someone, 'You are not human!'? Therefore, in order to overcome this 'evil tendency' of mass literature, there is no other way than to create healthy popular literature."

Because Kisaki Sanji's advocacy contains the issue of popularizing literature, Nao Tokunaga stood up to oppose him, saying that he was advocating a vulgarized literature massification theory. He further argued that "veritable record literature" cannot be literature with lower artistic qualities, but must also be artistic literature. This artistic literature is only historical subject matter.

Regarding this issue, not many people are participating in the discussion at present, so as for what it should ultimately be, we can only wait and see.

Rest 222

— Zheng Hua

Lying under the shade of the willow, wiping away sweat, stretching out my legs only to feel them ache, looking up at the blue sky and taking a deep breath of relief, wondering if there is any sign of rain in the floating clouds? Putting the dry tobacco pipe in my mouth, closing my eyes, a gust of fresh wind disperses the tiredness from my face, turning over, patting the dust off my body, and bursting forth with new strength, struggling to stand up.

University Days (18) 223

— Written by German Tomo, Translated by Chen Yin Zhi

But at this time, I probably walked into a depression, because the air became quieter, and I walked for a long time among the dense hawthorn trees. Sometimes, when a slight breeze arose, I smelled a burst of strong fragrance, but I didn't know where it came from, because the bushes on both sides blocked my view. The boundary dike on the right suddenly turned back, and a small barren area in the shape of a hill was presented in front of me. Raspberries and blackberries grew all over the ground; in the center, next to a stream of black spring water, a slender tree stood alone in the bright sunlight. Countless white flower balls emerged from the tree's dazzling green leaves. Whether in the city garden or in the distant forest, I had never seen such a delicate scene. I watched the tree in amazement, standing in this quiet place as if it were a miracle.

The section of the road ahead, with only a few sparse fields separating me, was the large brown wilderness, stretching forward to where the eye could not see; the outermost boundary of the ground trembled in the air. Not a person, not an animal, could be seen within the range of sight. —I lay in the grass next to the spring, under the shade of this beautiful tall tree. A sweet, mysterious feeling invaded me; the wild finches sang softly in the distance like a dream, the wild bees buzzed in the stamens above my head; sometimes the breeze blew, and a burst of floral fragrance came to me; other than that, everything was silent, even to the farthest places. I saw butterflies dancing beside the spring water; but I didn't pay attention to them now, my butterfly net lay lazily beside me.—I remembered a painting I saw not long ago. In a vast, boundless background, just like here, a young shepherd stood leaning on a shepherd's staff, like humans just after creation, a rough goatskin often used as an apron, binding his lower body; at his feet, sat a beautiful little girl, his eyes drooping to look at her; she watched the quiet scenery under the morning sun with happiness and without thought, with her black and large eyes.—Under the picture were written the words "Alone in the World."—I closed my eyes; I imagined a second person coming from the void to my side, and with her, all my needs ceased, and all my desires were satisfied. "Nali!" I called softly, and stretched my arms out into the gentle air.

At this time, the sun had already set, and the evening glow in front of me was shining on the wilderness. There was no sound on the tree anymore, and the wild bees had all flown away. It was time to go home. My hand grasped the butterfly net. But what use was this thing to me now? I jumped up and hung the butterfly net on the tree, as high as I could reach on the leafy branches, and then, the portrait of the tailor's beautiful daughter swayed before my drunken eyes, and I slowly walked home like this.

Dusk had already fallen deeply when I stepped out of the garden gate of the mansion. Outside the gate, the wooden horse carousel, was already lit; the sound of the accordion, laughter, and the noise of people, I could hear them all, and in the middle there was also the sound of fake swords clashing against iron rings. I stood, looking through the linden trees that surrounded the square, watching the rotating shadows. The wooden horse carousel was spinning vigorously; the seats and the wooden horses were all occupied, and a large crowd of old and young, male and female, were crowded around watching. Now it was turning slower and slower, and I could already recognize a few figures from between the green leaves.

A Glimpse of the Vegetable Market (Continued) 224

— Hei Ying

Turning around, the smiling face of a Javanese woman greeted me:

"Nyonya, my ulam (note) is fresh, look—"

"I'm very sorry, I'm not eating it today—"

"Oh…"

So the Javanese woman sat back down on the cement floor, dealing with other people's business.

There were many people in the pasar, arguing over their prices in various different languages. A newcomer from Tangshan (China) was clashing with the pockmarked Malay man because they couldn't agree on the price. The newcomer was being cursed with the most vulgar words. Our neighbor, the sister-in-law, stopped to chat with her aunt, talking endlessly about her household chores. A Malay child's mouth was close to my ear, mumbling: "We're going swimming at ×××, do you want to come—" Seeing his aunt turn her face around, he quickly slipped away.

There was a 60-year-old Xinhui man selling his vegetables in the corner of the pasar. My aunt said, "This Xinhui uncle's son and daughter-in-law farm in the vegetable garden, carrying the green vegetables early every morning for him to sell." And she praised his green vegetables as being better than other people's.

"Xinhui uncle, you're old, when are you going back to Tangshan?" Some people who were doing business with him casually chatted with him like this.

"Are you talking about going back to Tangshan to enjoy life?" Touching his white beard, he said with a smile, "My son hasn't made a fortune yet."

Another person put a pile of chili peppers on the weighing pan, asking him to see how much it weighed. So the Xinhui grandfather shifted his conversation back to the transaction.

The ice jelly wasn't ready yet, otherwise I could have asked my aunt for a few coppers. Seeing that there was nothing else to buy, "Let's go home!" She walked ahead again, and I followed behind carrying the heavy basket filled with fish and meat, green vegetables and broad beans.

And my cousin was already waiting in the kitchen.

I became lonely again, picked up the ukulele, and went under the mango tree to sing lonely songs. My cousin's young face often looked at me from the window; when I saw her, she stuck out her tongue again. With the most appropriate smile, I recalled that one night when my grandmother's illness reached a very dangerous point, she secretly called me to her bedside and said to me in a hoarse voice; "Little devil! Remember: If I unfortunately have to die tonight, I have nothing else to say, except that in the future, if your aunt comes up with the idea of marrying your cousin to you, for my sake, don't make a fuss, okay!" Like this, I wanted to bless my grandmother's health…

"Hey, hey, don't even want to eat rice? Little devil, what a strange fellow you really are!"

My aunt's voice woke me from my reverie. I scrambled to my feet and went back into the house to eat.

(Note) Ulam is a kind of food in Southeast Asia.

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Thoughts

Research on Places for Urinating 225

— Fang

Yesterday, I went to visit a friend at a certain place. On the way back, I walked to a certain wide road and was really desperate to urinate. So I dashed into a small alley because I was in a hurry, and I didn't have time to check its name. As soon as I entered the alley, I saw ten large characters written on the wall with kerosene, which read, "Urinating is prohibited here; offenders will be sent to the authorities."

But strangely enough, under these ten large characters, there were two or three people standing and urinating directly in front of them. I was helpless, so I also did an illegal thing. At first, I was a little suspicious, fearing that because I was desperate, my eyesight was blurry, so I misread it, or perhaps it was written, "Urinating is only allowed here; offenders will not be sent to the authorities." But after finishing, wiping my glasses, and looking carefully again, it was indeed correct.

I thought, why do we Chinese people specialize in doing things that violate laws and regulations? It is clearly written that urinating is prohibited here, so why do people insist on urinating in this place? I am deeply puzzled. Could it be that the meaning of writing these ten characters is to invite people to urinate here, with the intention of attracting customers? But urinating requires people to be able to urinate, unlike doing business, where you can write a sign saying "Welcome to Visit." What is the meaning of inviting people to urinate? It is certainly illogical. Therefore, I conducted an in-depth study on this urinating problem.

First, is it permissible to urinate in that place? Assuming that it is indeed not permissible to urinate, why are those who urinate there not arrested and sent to the authorities for investigation? If it is permissible to urinate there, why insist on writing these big characters to scare people?

Second, why do those who urinate insist on urinating in places where it is written "Urinating is prohibited"? Indeed, there are many places in alleys where it is written "Urinating is prohibited," but there are also places where it is not written. Why not go to places where it is not written "Urinating is prohibited" and urinate there? Why insist on going to places where it is written "Urinating is prohibited" to urinate? This is a very strange thing.

Is it a violation of laws and regulations, the inferior nature of our people? Or is this kind of prohibition inappropriate, and is it enough to arouse the psychology and habits of those who are anxious to urinate to violate laws and regulations? Therefore, those who urinate there are indeed mistaken. But those who write these ten big characters must also take it seriously and not write them casually.

Summer in the Ancient City 226

— Ji Zhuan

The rain poured down incessantly, hitting the clusters of thatched roofs, the sound like thousands of wild horses galloping. Coarse raindrops seeped into the houses from the roofs and loose earthen walls, and a kind of uncomfortable dampness filled these small, old, and desolate little houses. However, the souls sleeping in these houses, eroded by years and labor, slept even more peacefully and securely: this summer, it hadn't rained properly until the end of May, and people suffered in the sun all day long, unable to save even half a seedling in the fields. On this day, seeing the dense dark clouds, even the old Lianxin flowers were happy and smiled; the dream was so deep, the night was so long; in the dream, there grew boundless, fat, oily green rice stalks, and wheat waves rising with the breeze. Thus, the simple, hardworking, hopeful smile also opened in the dark night. "A good summer, an abundant summer, a peaceful and smooth summer!" People still thought so, still prayed so; no matter how dangerous this year was, how old and desolate this small city was, and how dim and terrible their destiny in this life was arranged.

The dim midday moon was obscured by layers of gray clouds, faintly illuminating

Page 20

the dilapidated ancient city with gray-white and weak light, illuminating the half-wilted crops in the fields, illuminating the old, water-stained, dripping dreams, illuminating the entire ancient city's summer.)

Lately, I feel that the soul is young, and life is fragile, so living aimlessly among people is a little scary! Because of this, I plan to arrange my life a little simpler, a little lighter, so I took advantage of this hot weather and quietly, without letting anyone know, slipped alone into this ancient city, which has become dilapidated and desolate following the progress of the era's pathology, and settled down; here, the soul of a person may gradually age along with the dilapidation and loneliness of this region.

There are about fifty households here, but most of the men in their prime are gone—after a series of disasters and hardships, the dead have died, and the living have gone, not knowing where. What remains are just some withered, ancient souls forgotten by death, living in a world they will never understand, letting gray-white ordinariness accompany them, and they, in turn, accompany those dim, dull days that come one after another.

However, I have finally settled down here; when I first came, there was just a bit of intermittent croaking of frogs in the pond, and the weather was already thoroughly hot: in the morning, before the sky was fully bright, clusters of crimson-gold clouds were horizontally stitched on the gray-white horizon, and a stream of golden light slowly rose, a good sun was already hanging in the sky, and the ground suddenly became hot. It had been a long time since there had been any rain, and these eroded souls were used to living in hardship, and anxiety was already too common for them. They just watched the dangerous situation in the fields, all day long hanging on the waterwheels, panting until they fainted. When it rained, people would perhaps be a little more excited to loosen the soil. Some small watermelons, planted in the corner of the field in the spring, grew plump soon after a rain. They were unwilling to eat them themselves, but picked them up and carried them on poles to the town to sell; in the evening, they put a plate of salted melons on the bamboo mat in the threshing ground, filled themselves with half-cooked bean and rice (in fact, it was already rare), looked at the stars in the sky, sighed, and countless mosquitoes buzzed around in circles. In that way, another day of life slipped by.

As the days crawled by, I felt that the summer in the ancient city was as old, depressed, and dilapidated as its residents.

Oh, the summer in the ancient city.

Seven Star Crags 227

— Ai Tu

It is summer, and the south, near the equator, must be very hot.

At this time of year, I think of my childhood life again. For example, when I was in the south, I would either run back to the quiet countryside or travel to a shady mountain forest. I really wouldn't be attached to the city, which is full of terrible heat and depressing atmosphere. - I admire the countryside!

One summer, I had the opportunity to go to Dinghu Mountain in Zhaoqing, and when I came back, I wandered around Zhaoqing city to the famous Seven Star Crags.

In the morning, the sun, which had not yet revealed its fiery heat, seemed like a lovely virgin, shyly wearing a pink coat, drifting like light sand, with a gentle and lovely smile, like a loving mother, descending on the quiet countryside and suburbs of the small market town. The old villages, distantly arranged in the mountains and fields, were also covered with bright red clothes. The whistle blown by the wind through the treetops of the jungle and the twittering songs of the little birds filled the air with pleasant atmosphere. The green leaves were also dyed with lovely colors, as if everything had become young and virginal.

We left the small market town and passed through the fields along a narrow road. The quiet river flowed murmuringly like a monotonous melody. The reeds on both sides were gently swaying in the wind. I opened my eyes wide and felt that the morning in the countryside was the most precious, fresh, and progressive. The dew on the vast fields reflected the morning sunlight, as clear as crystal.

We ran towards the black cave, passed many hills and crossed small rivers, and met many interesting village children, who were all jumping around barefoot, so innocent. And they would stare at us with surprised eyes, laughing strangely.

On the way, after running for a while, the sun had lost its beautiful virgin face, and it was hanging high in the middle of the sky. Moreover, the earth had gradually reflected the fiery light, making people feel the heat of summer, and sweat quickly disappeared from their faces.

We came to a dilapidated temple, full of overgrown weeds, densely packed. It might be the large temple at the foot of Seven Star Crags, but after being ravaged by many storms, it had revealed a calm desolation, like a dejected person sighing. We stepped in with light steps and could not see a trace of incense, which made us feel frightened, so we quickly turned out, turned up the mountain peaks again, and slipped into the dark cave.

There are many myths about Seven Star Crags, but we don't care about them. We just want to tread through the dark and quiet water cave with the mood of explorers. Perhaps because this place is very cool, every summer, countless tourists come from the city, and they often don't want to leave.

In a winding and huge dry cave, there were temples and incense, which was very lively, but it became our "cannon firing" place, making the cave sound like a battlefield. Coming out of this cave, we slipped into a water cave like a black river. When we drove the small boat slowly into it, we gradually felt a sense of autumn coolness, even a sense of severe cold. That dark shadow was really scary. When we shone the electric light on the moist walls, we could see spots and traces of water hanging in the air. The sound of dripping was very clear and resentful. The natural artistic paintings were as fierce as executioners and as cruel as whips, all silent like death, making people feel infinitely sad. When we felt cold, we quickly turned the boat back along the original road. - It's really not good to linger in a sunless hell!

After wandering through such a cave, the evening sun shone and sent us back.

— Hu Kao

Let me tell you, there are still such prostitutes in Shanghai!

White Orchids 228

— Xiao Hong

Every morning, just as I woke up from my sleep and was turning over the newspaper of the day on the bed, a silver bell-like sound floated in the quiet long alley:

"Do you want white orchids, beaded flowers..."

Every day, every day, the silver bell-like flower-selling sound called out from far to near, and then gradually disappeared in the air from near to far, like a fickle dream that is difficult to grasp, recalling the fresh traces from the blur, and then turning from fresh to blur.

Occasionally, because I woke up early, when I finished reading the newspaper, I couldn't hear the silver bell-like cry, and I would feel uneasy in my heart, "Why hasn't the flower seller come yet?" It was as if I had a premonition that something unfortunate had happened to the flower girl with a silver bell-like voice.

It wasn't until that familiar sound floated from the alley that my heart settled down.

However, I have never bought a flower from her, and I don't even know what the flower seller looks like. I just lie in bed every day and admire that silver bell-like voice.

It wasn't until this happened that I bought a white orchid from her every day, and I still do...

Every day, yes, almost every day, as long as I had money, I would always spend my hard-earned passionate evenings in crazy jazz music. Besides dancing and drinking, passionate nights were unbearable for me.

Under the influence of alcohol and jazz music, I met a woman, a woman with bright eyes and dark eyelashes.

"Why do you always wear white orchids every day?"

"I like it."

"Is there any other reason?"

"No, just because I like it." After a while, again: "Oh, maybe because I can't afford perfume."

"You mean, if you had perfume, you wouldn't want to wear it."

"No, even if I had perfume, I would still wear it, I like it."

"Then why did you say it was because you couldn't afford perfume?"

"Isn't it the same as having a strong fragrance?"

I understood why she wore white orchids every day, and that day, she gave me one, and because it had been worn for a day, the tip of the leaf had turned yellowish-brown.

But I still cherished it and brought it back, hanging it on the head of a bronze Buddha on the desk.

The next day, the yellowish-brown color spread all over the petals. The third day, the fourth day, the fifth day... it had turned yellowish-brown and dried up.

But I didn't throw it away, I still let it hang on the head of the bronze Buddha. Because this is the best explanation for a dancer.

Since this happened, I have been buying white orchids every day, and I still do.

Now, I not only admire the silver bell-like flower-selling sound, but I also spend a few cents every day to enjoy the rich fragrance of white orchids.

And occasionally, on mornings when I wake up early, when I don't hear that silver bell-like flower-selling sound, it will especially cause me uneasiness and disappointment.

Dusk 229

— Ye Bin

I selected a boxed novel from the bookshelf, lay down on the sofa, reluctantly calmed the boredom in my heart, and slowly opened the toothpick to pull out the book with the colored cover.

The cover was a statue of a girl, dyed in color, a photo from the hand of a high-end photographer. She had recently taken a liking to photography, and famous photo studios kept one or several of her negatives, but none of them were satisfactory to her. On the colored paper walls of her bedroom, various styles of picture frames hung down, which were artistic photographs cut out from pictorials, or Hollywood movie stars, which were photos that satisfied her; but none of them were her own.

She bought back the boxed novel because she liked the colored girl statue on the cover. In the bookstore, she wanted to tear it off, but the clerk quickly wrapped it up. It was almost dusk when she returned home. Under the milky white electric light, she opened the toothpick of the box again. With a hysterical impulse, she couldn't bear to let her own fingers destroy the beautifully bound book, although she intended to let the colored girl statue occupy a place on the wall.

She carefully placed it on the bookshelf, which was really frustrating.

She was sick for two weeks, a disease that doctors could not diagnose. Her mother loved this only daughter, and the famous doctors did not work. She advised her daughter to stay in the hospital. She even gave many examples, as if the hospital could cure diseases that doctors could not handle. The daughter understood medicine even better. She asked her mother not to come to her room to talk too much, and forbade others to disturb her need for a quiet heart: she could heal her own illness.

The mother did not understand her daughter's "medical skills." She stopped eating and sleeping, eavesdropping outside her daughter's bedroom door, or peeking through the keyhole. The daughter was sleeping quietly, and there was no sound in the room, as if it were a harbinger of an unfortunate event. But the mother knew her daughter's temper.

The daughter recovered from her illness, and the mother was relieved.

On the first day she got out of bed, she thought of the colored girl statue on the cover. When she slowly pulled out the book, she found worm-eaten marks on the girl's face. This made her very angry, and she tore up her beloved picture for the first time.

Like spring butterflies, colorful pictures flew in the air.

She stood up and walked to the window, opened the patterned long gauze curtains. Outside the window was the plum rain season, with fine slanting rain, as fluttering as her heart.

Her father's car came out from the garage, passed through the paved road lined with wintergreen, and drove towards the gate. She saw the shadows of her father and aunt reflected in the rear window.

She thought of her own marriage:

Her father was a reputable businessman in Shanghai, and what he was concerned about was economic manipulation and the improper development of his own business. Family, wife, daughter, he seemed not to need them. He put some banknotes on his mother's bedside every month and fulfilled his obligations as master, husband, and father. The marriage of his daughter, in his mind of whoring and taking concubines, there was no space to put this unimportant responsibility. The mother was born as a daughter. She entrusted the driver, the hairdresser... to choose a suitable husband for her daughter. She earnestly sought opinions from people and gods, but not from her daughter herself. Since her husband had abandoned her and she had no son, her standard for choosing a son-in-law was to meet all the ordinary conditions of a mother without a son.

But when the conditions did not meet her ideals, the daughter's age increased alarmingly.

She could no longer support her shaking blood pressure, and collapsed into the sofa chair in front of the dressing table. The mirror reflected her gray and yellow face of a young girl whose youth had passed away.

The mother quietly pushed the door open and asked.

"Mei, are you better today?" As gentle as a lover's whisper, "Bird's nest soup is cooked."

Leaning against the bedroom door, waiting for her daughter's reply, or a slight nod from her daughter, she could immediately step back out and bring in a bowl of freshly cooked bird's nest.

The daughter had never been a mother, and she did not know her mother's loyalty to her children, and she did not do what her mother hoped for.

"Mom, I don't like sweet things, it's too greasy to vomit!" The daughter shook her head, "Mom, you eat it."

The mother deliberately smiled.

"Yes. It's really annoying when the yellow plum rain doesn't stop! Mei, let's ask a doctor to see you tomorrow." After she made this suggestion, she was afraid that her daughter would object, so she immediately added: "My back also aches, probably because of some seasonal changes, and I have to take some medicine."

Clenching her fists, she gently tapped her lower back with her backhand, and went out of the room.

The daughter glanced at the colorful paper scraps on the ground, closed her eyes, and wanted to drive all the painful phenomena out of the door like her mother.

Outside the window, the rain became denser, and it was dusk again.

From "Nora" to "Statue of Liberty" 235

"Nora" is not a problem drama in the current stage; but at the moment when women all over the world are asked to return to the kitchen and to the puppet family, it still has a special meaning. Especially after the joint performance of amateur actors at the Jincheng Theater, it raised a memorandum to the silent Chinese women's movement. However, the impression this play gives them is what Nora did after she ran away, which will make them terrified, trembling, and hesitant. In Gladkov's "Cement", Dasha, who grew up in a life of hardship, has already had a correct answer. As for Situ Huimin's "Statue of Liberty", which was compiled and directed by Diantong, it actively and correctly pointed out that Nora, who ran away, was not wandering on a forked road, but training herself to be an independent and dignified person, serving the society.

Yanyan plays Ruo Yan in "Tianlun". After divorcing her husband, she became a sad and happy woman.
